## Domain Knowledge (LLM-generated)
**Domain**: chemical reaction kinetics
**Analysis**: This task models the rate of concentration change dA/dt in a chemical reaction. Classical rate laws express dA/dt as a function of concentration A (via power-law or rational forms), with possible explicit time dependence suggesting non-autonomous kinetics such as photolysis, time-varying catalysis, or sequential reaction mechanisms.

**Common formula structures in this domain**:
- Zero-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 (constant rate, independent of concentration)
- First-order decay: dA_dt = c0 * A (radioactive decay, unimolecular decomposition)
- Second-order decay: dA_dt = c0 * A**2 (bimolecular reaction of same species)
- nth-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A**c1 (general power-law rate law)
- Mixed-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A + c1 * A**2 (competing first and second order)
- Michaelis-Menten type: dA_dt = c0 * A / (c1 + A) (enzyme-catalyzed or saturation kinetics)
- Autocatalytic reaction: dA_dt = c0 * A * (c1 - A) (logistic-type autocatalysis)
- Time-dependent first-order: dA_dt = c0 * A * exp(c1 * t) (time-varying rate constant, e.g., photolysis with varying light)
- Photolysis with decay: dA_dt = c0 * A * exp(c1 * t) + c2 * A (combined photolytic and thermal decomposition)
- Time-modulated rate: dA_dt = c0 * A * (c1 + c2 * t) (linearly time-varying rate coefficient)
- Power-law with time factor: dA_dt = c0 * A**c1 * t**c2 (fractal or anomalous kinetics)
- Inhibition kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A / (c1 + A)**2 (substrate inhibition)
- Reversible reaction: dA_dt = c0 * A + c1 * (c2 - A) (forward-reverse equilibrium approach)
- Cooperative kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A**c1 / (c2 + A**c1) (Hill-type cooperative binding/reaction)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope ‚Üí Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects ‚Üí Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay ‚Üí Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior ‚Üí Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects ‚Üí Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Rate proportional to concentration power ‚Üí Power-law rate law dA_dt = c*A**n indicates reaction order n
- Rational function of concentration ‚Üí Saturation or enzyme kinetics (Michaelis-Menten, Langmuir-Hinshelwood mechanism)
- Product of A and (constant - A) ‚Üí Autocatalytic or logistic growth behavior in reversible/self-catalyzed reactions
- Explicit time dependence multiplied by concentration ‚Üí Non-autonomous kinetics such as photochemical reactions or externally modulated conditions
- Sum of terms with different powers of A ‚Üí Competing parallel reaction pathways with different orders
- Exponential in time multiplying A ‚Üí Time-varying activation energy or temperature ramp experiments (non-isothermal kinetics)
- Negative rate with A squared plus positive constant term ‚Üí Approach to equilibrium in reversible bimolecular reactions
- Fractional power of time (t**c) ‚Üí Anomalous or diffusion-limited kinetics in heterogeneous media
- Ratio of polynomials in A ‚Üí Surface-catalyzed reactions following Langmuir-Hinshelwood or Eley-Rideal mechanisms
